This consent applies to all Norton Healthcare physician practice and Immediate Care Center locations.

been given byanyone asto the results that may be obtained This consent includes testing for Hepatitis, Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HTV) ot any other blood-borne infectious
diseases, ifordered for diagnostic purposes or due to an occupational exposure. I consent to photographing, videotaping, video monitoring and audio devices for medical, scientific,

me will only bereleased when authorized byme or asneeded to provide for my continued medical treatment or identification.

Audio Recording and Transcription Consent Form —Clinical Documentation
documentation for your medical record. To ensure the accuracy and completeness of the record, your
provider will review the documentation, edit if necessary, and approve as final before it is entered into
your medical record
Norton uses a third-party service provider that is not affiliated with Norton to transcribe and produce
the clinical documentation for your medical record. Norton has appropriate agreements in place to
protect the confidentiality of your information. The transcript is kept within the application for a short
period of time, then it is destroyed and cannot be recovered.
Using this new technology supports our mission of Providing high quality care to our patients by
reducing the amount of time providers spend on documentation, which allows them to spend more
time caring for their patients.
This consent is voluntary, and your care will not be conditioned on providing consent to this new technology.

MyChart Telemedicine Informed Consent
Electronic signature on [DOB-1] 10:34 AM (effective from [DOB-1] expires [DOB-2]) - E-signed
Generated on 1/2/25 9:31 AM Page 6
Patient Name: Ditto,Micheal Vincent Jr.
Norton Healthcare Telemedicine Informed Consent Date Of Birth: 4/7/2023
MRN: EP02860650
I understand that telemedicine is the use of electronic information and communication technologies by a health care provider to
deliver services to an individual when he/she is located at a different site than the provider; and hereby consent to Norton
Healthcare providing health care services to me via telemedicine. The information discussed maybe used for diagnosis, therapy,
follow-up and/or education.
Expected Benefits:
*Improved access to care by enabling a patient to obtain services from providers at distant sites.
¢Patient remains closer to home where local healthcare providers can maintain continuity ofcare.
*Reduced need to travel for the patient or other provider.
The Process:
You will be introduced to the provider, such as residents, fellows, medical students and/or students of various health care fields who
are not employees of Norton Healthcare. You may ask questions of the provider or any telemedicine staff in the room with you, ifyou
are unsure ofwhat is happening. If you are not comfortable with seeing a provider on videoconferencing technology, you may reject
the use ofthe technology and schedule a traditional face-to-face encounter at any time. Safety measures have been implemented to
ensure that this videoconference is secure, and no part ofthe encounter will be recorded without your written consent.
Possible Risks:
There are potential risks associated with the use oftelemedicine which include, but may not be limited to:
¢A provider may determine that the telehealth encounter is not yielding sufficient information to make an appropriate clinical
decision.
*Technology problems may delay medical evaluation and treatment for your encounter.
*In very rare instances, security protocols could fail, causing a breach ofprivacy ofpersonal medical information.
By Signing this Form, I understand the following:
1. I understand that the laws that protect privacy and confidentiality of medical information also apply to telemedicine, and that no
information obtained in the use oftelemedicine which identifies me will be disclosed to researchers or other entities without my
consent.
2. I understand that I have the right to withdraw my consent to the use of telemedicine in the course of my care at any time, without
affecting myright to future care or treatment.
3. also understand that ifthe provider believes I would be better served by atraditional face-to-face encounter, they may, at any
time stop the telemedicine visit and schedule a face-to-face visit.
4. I understand that I may expect the anticipated benefits from the use oftelemedicine in my care, but that no results can be
guaranteed or assured.
Patient Consent to the Use of Telemedicine:
I have read and understand the information provided above regarding telemedicine, and all ofmy questions have been answered to
my satisfaction. I hereby give my informed consent for the use of telemedicine in my care.
I hereby authorize Norton Healthcare to use telemedicine in the course ofmy diagnosis and treatment.

*Congenital Adrenal Hyperplasia-1 7OHP normal weight-based limits for all initial specimens and repeat specimens on infants less than one week old: <1500g, <70 ng/mL; 1500g-2500g, <40 ng/mL

negative results.
**TSH and T4- These assays have received FDA clearance with intended use as an aid inscreening newboms forcongenital hypothyroidism only. TSH values below 2.91, the lower limitof linearity
for this method, will be reported as <2.91. T4 values below 2.5, the lower limit of linearity for this method, will be reported as <2.5. Rare hypothalamic and pituitary disorders may be causes of feta
hypothyroidism with low TSH and low T4

specimens (regardless of age) is <50 ng/mL. Meconeum Ileus may result in false negative results.

Point: Prevent Breast Engorgement (Done)
feeding on cue and keeping the breasts empty. If the baby is unable to latch correctly to a full breast, the breast can be
softened by using a warm compress, warm shower or placing the breasts in a tub of warm water. If the above doesn't work, another 
way to soften the breast is to pump a small amount.
Point: Manual Expression (Done)
-Lower risk for sudden infant death syndrome
-Lower risk for being overweight and having diabetes later in life
Benefits for mothers: -Convenient -Saves money
-Increases bonding with baby
-Helpful with weight loss
-Less bleeding after baby is born
-Reduces risk for depression after childbirth
-Lowers risk for diabetes, high cholesterol, heart disease and stroke
-Decreases risk for breast and ovarian cancer
Source: American Academy of Pediatrics Policy Statement “Breastfeeding and the Use of Human Milk” Learning Progress Summary

pumping. Demonstrate using both single and double pumping.

[DOB-7] - Admission (Discharged) in NWC 4E Neonatal Intensive Care (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Topic: Nutrition/Hydration (Done)
Point: TPN (Done)
nutrition from the foods they eat. TPN always goes into the vein (blood vessel) through an intravenous (IV) line. It may be given
in the hospital, long-term care center, or at home. A patient may need TPN for several days or longer. This will be
decided by your caregiver.
Point: Tube Feeding (Done)
nutritional formulas can be inserted into the stomach (G-tubes), into the jejunum of the small intestine (J-tubes), through the
nose and into the stomach (NG-tubes), or through the nose and into the small intestine (NJ tubes). The NG and NJ tubes are
considered to be temporary and the G tube and J tube is considered more permanent but it can be removed. With all tube
feeding approaches, if a person is able, he/she may continue eating and drinking while the tube feeding provides the consistent
caloric intake needed for weight maintenance or gain. Thus oral intake can be continued for more pleasurable sensations, such
as small bites of a favorite food.
Point: Nutrition/Hydration Consumption (Done)

Patient Education (continued)
Topic: Infection Prevention (Done)
Point: Intake and Output (Done)
Point: Multi-drug Resistant Organism (Done)
Explain that an MDRO is a strain of bacteria that is resistant to common antibiotics used to treat infections. Infections can vary, depending on the organism. MDROs can cause skin infections (boils, abscesses), urinary tract infections, blood stream
infections, and pneumonia, and they can infect wounds, the respiratory tract and surgical sites.
Point: Central Line Infection Prevention (Done)
accessing line
to clean hands and scrub the hub before accessing.

[DOB-7] - Admission (Discharged) in NWC 4E Neonatal Intensive Care (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Follow all instructions on signs posted in the patient care area. You may be asked to wear gowns, gloves
mask or shoe covers while with the patient. You are asked to wear these items to protect your clothing and
body from possible germs that could be spread from person to person. You should remove these isolation
items before leaving the patient's room and then ALWAYS clean your hands so you do not spread any
germs throughout the hospital.
Point: Protect Others from Infection (Done)
Point: Protect Yourself from Further Infection (Done)
Point: Isolation Precautions (Done)
Point: Catheter Care (Done)

Description:
Educate on respiratory hygiene and cough etiquette. To protect from further infection and to protect others from getting an
infection, patient should cover nose and mouth with tissues when coughing. Encourage patient to place used tissues in a
plastic bag that will not allow secretions to soak through. Patient should always wash their hands after using or handling
used tissues.

During a typical blood transfusion, certain parts of blood are delivered through an intravenous (IV) line that's placed in the
patient. A blood transfusion usually takes two to four hours, though in an emergency it can be done much faster. A blood transfusion boosts blood levels that are low, either because the body isn't making enough or because blood has been
lost during surgery, injury or disease

Medication Information for After Discharge (continued)
How to transfer refills on a prescription:
¢ If you have refills on a prescription and would like to fill them at a different pharmacy: take your bottle(s) with the
prescription information to the pharmacy where you wish to have them filled. Or you can call the pharmacy where
you wish to fill them and notify them you would like to transfer your prescription(s). You will need to provide them
with information located on the bottle.
* To assure you do not miss doses, notify the pharmacy 2 to 3 days before you will run out.
How to get refills on medications that were started in the hospital:
¢ Itis common for doctors that discharge you from the hospital to only provide you with a short duration of
medication(s).
¢ This does not mean that you do not need to stay on the medication(s), but they want you to be seen by your
primary doctor to assess how you are doing and determine if you should stay on the same medication(s).
¢ It is very important that you have an appointment with your primary doctor within 30 days of discharge. At your
appointment, be sure to take any new medications with you and ask them to provide you with new prescriptions if
they feel you need to stay on them.
Safe medication storage and disposal
Medications should be stored by patients in secure locations and excess pills should be disposed of properly, to minimize
the risk of diversion and inappropriate use. To find a prescription drug disposal location near you please visit https://
odcp.ky.gov
If Prescribed Narcotic Medications:
Your providers may have already given you your prescription for pain medication prior to your discharge date. If this is the
case, it is best to be prepared and have your medication filled and ready for your return home from the hospital. You may
want to have your pain pills with you on your ride home if you are traveling a long distance.
While at Home:
¢ Use medication only as directed.
« Remember medication takes time to work. Most oral pain relievers need at least 20 minutes to take effect.
¢ Remember to take your pain medication before activity and at bedtime. Your provider may advise you to take your
pain medication at regular intervals (such as every 4 to 6 hours).
¢ Be sure to get enough rest. If you are having trouble sleeping, talk to your provider.
¢ Use pillows to support you when you sleep and when you do your coughing and deep breathing exercises
* Try using the alternative methods such as heating pads or cold therapy, walking, guided imagery tapes, listening
to soft music, changing your position in bed, aromatherapy, and massage can help relieve your pain.
Third Party Apps and Epic
Patients of providers that use Epic software are able to configure 3rd party apps to retrieve parts of their health record for
their own personal use, including lab results, allergies, medications, and immunization history.
For instructions, visit: https://open.epic.com/Tutorial/PatientAuthentication.
Your Same Day Care Options
We're committed to providing same-day care options, close to home, with the ease of online scheduling. Receive care with
a Norton Healthcare provider in person at one of our primary care, Norton Immediate Care or Norton Prompt Care at
Walgreens locations, or schedule a virtual visit with Norton eCare from the comfort of home. Access all of your care
options at NortonNow.com.

Your Same Day Care Options (continued)
Norton Care Call
If you are going home after leaving a hospital overnight stay, you may receive a Norton Care Call.
¢ Within 48 hours of discharge, you may receive an automated phone call from [PHONE-36] (Caller ID will read Norton
Care Call)
e The automated call will ask you a few questions about your health and progress. Please answer the questions using the
phone keypad.
¢ If your responses indicate you need additional assistance, a Norton Healthcare team member will call you back to offer
help and other instructions. Because our return calls are specific to your individual care, the returning call phone
number will be from a different Norton phone number. Please answer this call so we can best support your health and
progress.
Medical Records
Request medical records through MyNortonChart by using the Ask Customer Service feature or complete an authorization
form at https://medicalrecordrequest.nortonhealthcare.org
Requests are processed within 7 business days of receipt.

Instructions
Infant Instructions:
¢ Avoid Cigarette/All Smoke
* Keep Infant Warm
¢ Support Head At All Times
¢ Use of Approved CarSeat
Infant Care:
¢ Air Reddened Buttocks
¢ Bathe with Mild Soap/Water
¢ Infant on Back to Sleep
¢ Ointment to Red Buttocks
¢ Supervised Awake Tummy Time
¢ Avoid crowds such as church, malls, concerts, etc. for 4-6 weeks to allow baby’s immune system to mature. Ask family
and friends to refrain from visiting if they are ill, or have been exposed to someone who is.
¢ Ask all visitors to wash hands or use hand sanitizer
No Tub Baths Until Circumcision is Healed and Umbilical Cord has Fallen Off
Call Your Doctor For Problems:
¢ Makes Breathing Noises
* Continuous Coughing
¢ Chest Heaving/Pulling In
¢ Breathing Very Fast
¢ Colored Drainage from Eyes, Ears, and/or Nose
* Acts Listless
¢ Axillary temp less than 97 or greater than 100
¢ Vomiting and diarrhea
¢ Poor feeding
¢ "Something is just not right"
Hearing Screen: Left Pass;Right Pass, (04/11/23 1125)
Newborn screen: Done (completed 4/10), (04/11/23 0700)
Repeat Newborn Screen:
Circumcision: Done, (04/11/23 1200)
Car Seat Test: n/a
CCHD: 4/12/23 pass

Congratulations on your new baby! An ALGO AABR hearing screen is provided to all infants as
a Standard of care at our facility.
Results: L-EAR: pass ) / FAIL
R-EAR: PASS \ | FAIL
Sn i )
You will receive a brochure that describes infant speech and language development. Please
read this brochure and use it to record your infant's progress. If you are concerned that your
baby is not responding normally, please contact your child's primary care provider or an
audiologist. Hearing can be tested reliably at any age by an audiologist. Changes in hearing
can be detected early and should be treated promptly to protect your baby’s hearing health.
lf your baby did not pass today's hearing Screen, we will send baby's screening results to the
doctors ar Norton Children's ENT & Audiology. When they have received your baby's
information, they will call you to set up an appointment. If you have not heard from them in
three (3) business days after your discharge from the hospital, please call them at [PHONE-38] to set Up an appointment.
If you have any questions or would like more information, please do not hesitate to call the
newborn care technicians at Norton Women's and Children's Hospital at [PHONE-39].
Best,

EHDI Advisory Board Recommended Follow-Up for Children with Risk Factors for Hearing Loss (Updated
3/2022):
* Parental concern regarding hearing, speech, language, or developmental delays.
e Family history of permanent childhood hearing loss; first or second degree relative with onset prior to
age 18. Specify
e NICU stay greater than 5 days for any reason; Extracorporeal membrane oxygenation (ECMO);
Ototoxic medication —loop diuretics (furosemide), gentamycin, vancomycin, streptomycin,
cisplatin, carboplatin—up to 5 days duration total (not consecutive); Hyperbilirubinemia 218 mg/dl
or requiring exchange transfusion.
e Cleftlip/palate, atresia/microtia, other craniofacial anomalies or physical findings associated with
hearing loss. Specify
e Confirmed.diagnosis of in utero/congenital infections including Herpes, Rubella, Syphilis,
Toxoplasmosis, cytomegalovirus (CMV), or Zika.
* Confirmed or suspected culture positive infections associated with SNHL (meningitis/encephalitis),
viral and/or bacterial. :
e Confirmed or suspected syndromes associated with hearing loss or progressive/late-onset hearing
loss including, but not limited to: neurofibromatosis, osteopetrosis, and Usher syndrome; other
frequently identified syndromes including: Waardenburg, Alport, Pendred, and Jervell and LangeNielson.
* ° Neurodegenerative disorders, such as Hunter syndrome, or sensory motor neuropathies, such
as Friedreich ataxia. and Charcot-Marie-Tooth syndrome.
e Final refer (fail) inpatient newborn hearing screening (NBHS)
e Chemotherapy
e Head trauma
e Other severe medical conditions includingpersistent newborn pulmonary hypertension (PPHN),
hydrocephalus, perinatal asphyxia; hypoxic ischemicencephalopathy.

| understand the following about the use of the NicView™ viewing camera:
« | amresponsible for the user name and password provided to me. No other users will have access to
my infant's video unless | give them the username and password.
e Internet access is needed to view my infant with the NicView™ camera. Norton Healthcare is not
responsible for providing me with an internet access device or internet service.
e Recordings and/or copies of any NicView™ streaming image(s) are expressly forbidden.
¢ NicView™ is a streaming device and does not save or store any images, video or parent information.
¢ The purpose of the NicView™ viewing camera is to view my infant. The streaming images will be
turned off while my infant is receiving care. Norton Healthcare and the medical team have the right
to turn off the NicView™ at such times Norton Healthcare or the medical team deems appropriate.
¢ Information will be gathered related to use of the NicView™ camera, including how often it is
accessed and for how long. The information will be available to Norton Healthcare and to NATUS
Medical INC, the NicView™ system owner.
* [may not be able to view my infant during times when technical problems occur with the NicView™
camera or software.
* NATUS is responsible for any technical problems. | have been given the company’s support email
address and phone number.
+ If my infant is moved out of a hospital bed that has a NicView™ camera, |may not be able to view my
infant unless a mobile camera is available, and a NicView™ camera may be available to me only for
a limited period of time so that other families may be accommodated.
Expiration date —This consent expires when my infant is discharged from Norton Healthcare.
Withdrawal of consent — | understand that | may revoke the consent at any time.
